### Question 63: How does the P/NP grade work?  
### Answer: 

The P/NP (Pass/No Pass) grading system works as follows:

1. **Eligibility**: Students can choose to take up to 8 credits (usually 2 courses, each worth 4 credits) per academic year on a Pass/No Pass basis. This decision must be made by submitting a Petition to Elect Pass/No Pass Grade form to the Registrar's Office before a specified deadline (4:00 PM on Friday of Week 4 during a 16-week term).

o The Registrar’s Office is responsible for converting to the P/NP after receiving the final grade submission by the instructor at the end of the term. o A grade of ‘C-’ or higher will be counted as a Pass. Courses graded with a Pass grade can be used to meet prerequisite requirements for next-level courses. o Any grade below a ‘C-’ will be counted as a No Pass. No credit is granted for this result. The NP grade will be shown on the Official Transcript. Courses with a NP grade cannot be used to meet prerequisite requirements for next-level courses. • I = Incomplete: If a student is unable to complete the work in a course because of illness, family emergency, or other exceptional circumstances (see Section 12), a temporary grade of ‘I’ (Incomplete) may be awarded by the faculty until unfinished course requirements are completed. ### Question 64: How many courses can I take as P/NP at maximum and how will it contribute to the official transcript GPA?  
### Answer: 

You can take a total of 8 credits (typically 2 courses, 4 credits each) in one academic year on a Pass/No Pass basis. Pass/No Pass grades do not contribute to the official transcript GPA. Therefore, they will not affect your official transcript GPA. However, a grade of 'C-' or higher will be counted as a Pass, and courses graded with a Pass grade can be used to meet prerequisite requirements for next-level courses. Any grade below a 'C-' will be counted as a No Pass, and no credit is granted for this result. The NP grade will be shown on the Official Transcript, but it cannot be used to meet prerequisite requirements for next-level courses.

For example, an exploratory course can also be counted as a major course for the corresponding major. However, the number of double-counted credits is often limited (e.g., see subsections 13.2 and 13.3). Additionally, any particular course can only be used to satisfy at most two requirements. For instance, if course X is cross-listed between major A and major B and tagged by minor C, then X can be used to fulfill the requirements of major A and major B, or major A and minor C, or major B and minor C. Triple counting is not allowed. 13.9  Maximal Length of Study Fulbright follows MOET regulations, which state that the maximum time to complete the program cannot exceed double the standard

### Question 65: I've failed the GWP due to personal reasons so will it count toward the 144 maximum credits I can have?  
### Answer: 

No, failing the GWP (General Writing Proficiency) will not count toward the 144 maximum credits you can have. The context provided does not mention a specific 144 maximum credit limit. Typically, such limits pertain to the total number of credit hours a student can earn, not to failed courses. Failing a course results in a grade of F, which counts as an attempted credit but not as an earned credit. You would need to retake the course to earn credit towards your degree requirements. Always consult with your Academic/Major Advisor for specific guidance regarding your situation.

Attempted credits are the credit hours students enroll in and are recorded in the transcript, regardless of whether they complete the courses or pass them. This includes all courses for which a student receives a grade, including withdrawals (W), incompletes (I), repeats (RP), and failures (F). See section 4 for more details on different types of grades. To graduate with an undergraduate degree from Fulbright, a student must earn a minimum of 128 credit hours.  The typical full-time course load is 16 credit hours per term or 4 courses of 4 credit hours each. In order to make standard progress toward completing the degree, students are required to register for no fewer than 12 credit hours and no more than 20 credit hours per term. Students who wish to take fewer than 12 or more than 16 credit hours in one term must submit the Petition for Alternative Course Load or

tagged. For instance, if major A requires certain courses from major B for out-of-area foundation, exploration, or applications of the major, and these courses are not cross-listed between A and B, they do not count toward the 8-credit limit. 1 In interdisciplinary minors, the requirements mainly consist of courses from other majors. These courses are usually not cross-listed with the minors and are referred to as 'tagged' by these minors. 13.4  Experiential Learning Requirements Experiential Learning can count toward elective or major requirements (upon advisor approval). Fulbright’s Experiential Learning Program (ELP) exists to create, standardize, and facilitate academic credit-bearing experiential learning experiences. All full-time, undergraduate, degree- seeking students must complete at least 04 credits and a maximum of 12 credits under the ELP as a graduation requirement. Current ELP streams are housed within Academic Affairs (AA), Career Services (CS), and Center for Entrepreneurship and Innovation

### Question 66: What and how do I get an Academic Warning?  
### Answer: 

To receive an Academic Warning, students who are not making satisfactory progress towards their degree, fall below a 2.0 GPA, or face issues related to attendance, participation, citizenship, or academic integrity can expect this. The process involves receiving an Academic Warning from the Registrar's Office, followed by an Academic Progress Meeting where a Learning Contract is created with specific conditions tailored to the individual situation. The Registrar's Office records this as a matter of file and follows up accordingly. If a student receives three official warnings, it could lead to more severe disciplinary actions like Academic Probation or Academic Suspension. This warning is the first step in addressing academic performance issues before they escalate.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 11]
as specified. 6.2 Academic Warning This is usually the first level of intervention for students who are not making satisfactory progress toward their degree and/or who fall below a 2.0 GPA, or for other reasons such as failure of attendance, participation, citizenship, or academic integrity. An Academic Warning is sent out by the Registrar’s Office. The student is required to attend an Academic Progress Meeting during which a Learning Contract will be created with specific conditions tailored to the individual situation. The Registrar's Office will be informed as a matter of record and follow-up. ACADEMIC STANDING: Academic standing refers to how well a Fulbright student is meeting the general expectations toward the fulfillment of their degree. There are four categories of academic standing. 6.1 Good Standing Students with a minimum of 2.0 GPA, who are not on academic or non- academic warning, probation, suspension, or dismissal, and who are in good standing financially, are considered in Good Standing. Only students in Good Standing may participate in off-campus programs and other opportunities as specified. 6.2 Academic Warning This is usually the first level of intervention for students who are not making satisfactory progress toward their degree and/or who fall below a 2.0 GPA, or for other reasons such as failure of attendance, participation, citizenship, or academic integrity. An Academic Warning is sent out by the Registrar’s Office. The student is required to attend an Academic Progress Meeting during which a Learning Contract will be created with specific conditions tailored to the

### Question 68: Can you provide me with some courses suggestion to take to major in Math?  
### Answer: 

Based on the information provided, here are some course suggestions to major in Math:

1. Foundation Courses:
   - Linear Algebra
   - Single Variable Calculus
   - Introduction to Statistics
   - Multivariable Calculus

2. Intermediate Courses:
   - Probability
   - Differential Equations
   - Discrete Mathematics
   - Numerical Analysis

3. Advanced Courses:
   - Advanced Statistics
   - Statistical Learning
   - Stochastic Calculus
   - Numerical Analysis
   - Optimization
   - Partial Differential Equations

4. Pure Mathematics Courses:
   - Abstract Algebra
   - Real Analysis

5. Elective Applied Courses:
   - Operations Research
   - Introduction to Quantitative Finance
   - Game Theory
   - The Economics of Corruption
   - Money and Banking
   - Economics of Inequality
   - Cost-Benefit Analysis
   - Market Design
   - Signal, Systems, and Control
   - Computer Vision
   - Introduction to Machine Learning
   - Algorithm
   - Statistical Learning
   - Introduction to AI

Remember, you should consult with an academic advisor for course selection and ensure that you do not double count courses for different requirements. For instance, Operations Research can only count for either 1 Advanced course or 1 Elective course, but not both. Also, you must take at least 1 Pure Mathematics course and at least 2 Intermediate and Advanced courses. Additionally, you might consider attending Research Seminars to gain insights into faculty's research and recent developments in mathematical research. If you plan to undertake a Capstone Project, it would be optional but could be a valuable experience. Good luck!

### Question 69: How to declare a major in Computer Science?  
### Answer: 

To formally declare Computer Science as their major, the student must complete at least two Computer Science courses, which can include MATH 202 - Discrete Math. This requirement ensures that students have a foundational understanding of key concepts in computer science before officially declaring the major. Additionally, students should review the full list of major requirements, including specific courses and credit hours, to ensure they meet all prerequisites for the Computer Science program. It's important to consult with an academic advisor to confirm the exact steps and any additional requirements specific to the institution. Completing these initial courses helps prepare students for the more advanced coursework and projects required in the major.

Fulbright’s Experiential Learning Program (ELP) exists to create, standardize, and facilitate academic credit-bearing experiential learning experiences. All full-time, undergraduate, degree- seeking students must complete at least 04 credits and a maximum of 12 credits under the ELP as a graduation requirement. ### Question 71: Can you give me the process of making a Capstone for graduation?  
### Answer: 

The process of making a Capstone for graduation typically involves two main stages: Capstone I and Capstone II.

In Capstone I, you will actively conduct research and refine your project proposal and plan. You will focus on gathering and organizing the information or other materials needed to realize your project. In some cases, students may begin the very initial stages of production (subject to your advisors' approval). For Capstone I, you might be expected to submit a revised project proposal, initial field journal extracts or a creative portfolio, a literature review or annotated bibliography, a sample chapter or introduction, or other materials to be decided on in consultation with your advisors.

At the beginning of the semester, you should meet with your advisor as early as possible and set a regular meeting schedule and expectations for submissions with a timeline. Midterm submission(s) could include a revised project proposal and/or research questions, initial close readings, field journal extracts, and first drafts or excerpts of creative writing. End-of-term submission could include a literature review or annotated bibliography, a sample chapter, introduction or preface, selections or excerpts of creative writing, or other materials to be decided on in consultation with your advisors.

Capstone II focuses more on production, whether it be writing, filming, or realizing an idea. You will continue working on your project and produce the final version. Capstone II will be assessed by a combination of your active participation in the advising processes and end-of-term submission. The end-of-term submission will demonstrate successful progress towards the final Capstone submission and satisfactory completion. 

The Capstone culminates with a formal defense and a final evaluation by two readers. Students work with a primary advisor and, to a lesser extent, a secondary advisor. The format and length of projects are flexible, within certain limits. This handbook explains each aspect of the Capstone experience so that you can plan ahead and know what to expect.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: History Capstone Handbook - 2025-26.pdf, Page: 9]
seminars you have completed) and want an opportunity to carry out a long-term research project. For such students, the Capstone year provides time and guidance that is unparalleled by any course or other opportunity at the undergraduate level. However, if you wish to graduate with distinction—an honorable goal— but you don’t particularly enjoy doing independent research, you may want to skip the Capstone and focus on GPA honors instead! Normally, the Capstone sequence begins in the Fall with Capstone I and ends in the Spring with Capstone II. It culminates with a formal defense and a final evaluation by two readers. Students work with a primary advisor and, to a lesser extent, a secondary advisor. The format and length of projects is flexible, within certain limits. This handbook explains each aspect of the Capstone experience so that you can plan ahead and know what to expect. 1.2. ### Question 72: What are the grades required to get a distinctive graduation?  
### Answer: 

To graduate with honors, students need an honor pass capstone, which requires a score of 90 to 100 according to the grading criteria provided in the context. Scores between 65 to 89 result in a standard pass, while scores lower than 65 result in a no pass. Therefore, the grades required to get a distinctive graduation (with honors) are 90 to 100.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 20]
potential advisors to prepare their applications. Capstone projects will be graded No Pass/Pass/Honors and must be evaluated by the supervising faculty at least one month before the end of the student’s graduating term. Students whose capstone is graded Honors will be awarded Graduation with Honors. 13.7  Special Requirements Vietnamese students are required to complete the extra credits to fulfill the requirements from the Ministry of Education and Training (MOET), including: • Military training course • Physical Education • Political courses These courses do not count toward the 128-credit requirement. All students for whom English is not their first language must take an English Assessment Test required by NECHE Accreditation. 13.8  Double Counting In satisfying degree requirements, some courses can be double-counted. ### Question 73: How can I graduate with Honor or lie within the top GPA?  
### Answer: 

To graduate with honors or lie within the top GPA, you need to achieve a final score of at least 90% for the Capstone project, which corresponds to a Pass with Honor grade. Additionally, maintaining high grades across all your courses and possibly earning an A or A- grade point average (GPA) would help ensure you lie within the top GPA. Achieving these standards demonstrates exceptional performance and dedication, which are crucial for graduating with honors. However, it's important to note that the GPA is calculated excluding any P/NP, I, W, or RP graded courses. Therefore, focus on excelling in your coursework and completing your Capstone project with distinction to maximize your chances of graduating with honors.

### Question 74: How many courses can I take with P/NP grade in total?  
### Answer: 

You can take a total of 2 courses with a Pass/No Pass grade in total. Each course is typically 4 credits, so together they amount to 8 credits.

All students for whom English is not their first language must take an English Assessment Test required by NECHE Accreditation. 13.8  Double Counting In satisfying degree requirements, some courses can be double-counted. For example, an exploratory course can also be counted as a major course for the corresponding major. However, the number of double-counted credits is often limited (e.g., see subsections 13.2 and 13.3). Additionally, any particular course can only be used to satisfy at most two requirements. For instance, if course X is cross-listed between major A and major B and tagged by minor C, then X can be used to fulfill the requirements of major A and major B, or major A and minor C, or major B and minor C. Triple counting is not allowed. 13.9  Maximal Length of Study Fulbright follows MOET regulations, which state that the maximum time to complete the program cannot exceed double the standard

There are two types of absences mentioned in the given text: general absences and excused absences due to university-sponsored events/activities. However, the text also briefly mentions military leave, which is considered a separate type of absence. So, there are three types of absences in total.

### Question 76: How many types of leave of absence are there and how can I have one?  
### Answer: 

There are three types of leave of absence: Personal Leave, Medical Leave, and Administrative Leave of Absence.

To have one, you need to follow these steps:
1. For Personal Leave, you must complete the Undergraduate Leave of Absence form and submit it at least three weeks prior to the leave or as soon as possible if circumstances don't allow.
2. For Medical Leave, you must also complete the Undergraduate Leave of Absence form and submit it along with the Fulbright Impact Assessment form and all medical supporting documents before the last day of class. This leave is based on the recommendation of a health services professional verifying the impact on your ability to complete academic activities.
3. For Administrative Leave of Absence, you must inform the Registrar's Office about your outstanding student account balance in an enrolled term without informing grades, which may result in an "F" or "W" grade depending on the exceptional circumstances and supporting documents provided. 

Remember, indefinite leaves are not permitted for any type of leave. Fulbright guarantees reinstatement to students following an approved leave of up to one academic year. Additionally, normally, students are not permitted to remain on campus during a period of absence from their studies. Students may return earlier by notifying the Registrar's Office at least eight weeks in advance of the returning term. Students who return and resume their studies at Fulbright are expected to complete their program without further interruption. The effective date of the Leave of Absence will be from the date of request submission if it's approved. By submitting the Leave of Absence request after Week 8 of the 16-week term (Fall & Spring) or after Week 4 of the 8-week term (Summer), students must be aware of the potential impact on their studies.

### Question 79: What is the school's policy on academic dishonesty, and how are violations handled?  
### Answer: 

The school's policy on academic dishonesty is outlined in the Code of Academic Integrity at Fulbright University Vietnam. Violations can lead to various consequences depending on the severity and frequency of the offenses. For minor infractions, students might face an additional Academic Progress Meeting and could be placed on Academic Probation, which typically lasts for a term and may result in an updated Learning Contract. If a student fails to meet the requirements while on probation, they could be placed on Academic Suspension. Suspensions are noted on the student's transcript and typically last for one term or one academic year. Students on suspension must meet with the Dean’s Office to establish conditions for readmission. A student can be suspended a maximum of two times; further violations would not result in suspension but could lead to more severe disciplinary actions. The capstone project, a significant component of the curriculum, is also subject to these regulations regarding academic integrity, including the proper use of generative AI. This ensures that all academic work adheres to high standards of honesty and originality.

### Question 80: What are the policies regarding retaking exams or improving grades?  
### Answer: 

The policies regarding retaking exams or improving grades are as follows:

1. Students are required to repeat core courses if they receive a grade of 'F' or a grade below 'C-' in courses that count toward their major or minor.

2. Students may retake a course if they have received a grade of 'D+', 'D', 'F', or 'NP' for the course, or if they have withdrawn and received a grade of 'W'.

3. In special cases, a student may request to retake a course after receiving a grade higher than a 'D+' following consultation with their academic/major advisor, the course instructor, and the Registrar's Office. This request must consider the course availability and capacity in the next academic term or year.

4. If a higher grade is achieved in the retake, it will be used in the GPA calculation, while the lower grade will be overwritten by the notation "RP" (meaning "repeated") and remain on the transcript.

5. A student may not retake the same course for the third time unless they failed the second time or if a specific grade is needed to meet major requirements.

6. Students should consult with their Academic/Major Advisor about their program plan before considering retaking a class for the third time.

7. For disputes regarding final grades, students should first discuss the matter with the course instructor. If unresolved, they can file an appeal through the Review of Final Grade Request form within five business days from the date the final grade is posted. The Registrar's Office will inform the Dean's Office, and if mediation fails, a panel review will be organized for an independent evaluation of the grade. In cases concerning the interpretation of a course policy, the Dean's Office will defer to the course syllabus whenever possible. Otherwise, they will make a final ruling on the matter. 

8. Grades for courses where a P/NP, I, W, or RP grade is awarded are excluded from the GPA calculation. 

9. At the end of each term, grade reports are available for viewing on the Fulbright One Stop portal, named Unofficial Transcript. Paper copies of grade reports, named Transcript of Records, can be issued by the Registrar's Office upon students' request.

### Question 81: How does the university accommodate students with chronic illnesses or personal emergencies that affect attendance?  
### Answer: 

The university accommodates students with chronic illnesses or personal emergencies that affect attendance through the process of applying for a medical leave of absence. Students must submit the Undergraduate Leave of Absence form and the Fulbright Impact Assessment form, along with all medical supporting documents, before the last day of class. The leave duration is determined in conjunction with the health services professional, the Registrar's Office, and the student. This accommodation ensures that students can manage their health conditions or personal emergencies while still being able to complete their academic responsibilities. However, indefinite leaves are not permitted. For university-sponsored events, students need to obtain approval from the Office of the Dean and Deans of Students and ensure they are in good academic standing and not on probation. In cases of emergencies, students might be granted an excused absence, but they are still responsible for making up any missed work. These accommodations aim to support students during challenging times while maintaining academic standards.

### Question 82: Are students allowed to use AI tools like ChatGPT for assignments? If so, under what conditions?  
### Answer: 

Students are allowed to use AI tools like ChatGPT for assignments, but under specific conditions. They must provide comprehensive documentation of its usage, including:

• Objective and Scope: Clearly define the reasons for utilizing generative AI and the specific elements of the project it contributes to.
• Tools and Platforms: Specify the AI tools, models, or platforms employed.
• Process and Methodology: Outline how AI will be incorporated, detailing which aspects of the project will be generated, improved, or altered with the use of AI.
• Ethical and Copyright Issues: Address the ethical and copyright concerns associated with using generative AI and how these will be addressed throughout the project.

This documentation promotes transparency, offers insight into AI's role in the creative process, and highlights the originality and human contributions to the project. Additionally, students must ensure compliance with Fulbright University Vietnam’s Code of Academic Integrity, including updates on the usage of generative AI. Presenting text, images, or other content created by others or by generative AI as your own work, even at the sentence level, is grounds for failure of Capstone I and/or Capstone II. Therefore, while AI tools like ChatGPT can be used, proper documentation and adherence to academic integrity guidelines are crucial. Students should also seek IRB approval if their project involves research. The approval process can be found at https://fulbright.edu.vn/irb/.

### Question 83: Where can I get support for mental health treatment?  
### Answer: 

You can get support for mental health treatment through various means mentioned in the context, such as participating in a Mental Health First Aid Training Program, engaging in a Community Survey on Mental Health Needs, or taking part in a Public Art Project on Mental Health Themes. These initiatives aim to address mental health needs within the community and provide resources and awareness. However, for direct treatment, it is recommended to consult local mental health services as detailed in the Resource Guide for Local Mental Health Services. Always ensure to seek professional advice for personalized support and treatment options. The context does not explicitly mention specific treatment facilities or direct therapy services, so it's important to explore these resources alongside professional guidance.

Fulbright’s Experiential Learning Program (ELP) exists to create, standardize, and facilitate academic credit-bearing experiential learning experiences. All full-time, undergraduate, degree- seeking students must complete at least 04 credits and a maximum of 12 credits under the ELP as a graduation requirement. Current ELP streams are housed within Academic Affairs (AA), Career Services (CS), and Center for Entrepreneurship and Innovation (CEI), where each team is responsible for administrative and academic duties of their respective stream(s). The ELP operates within Fulbright’s undergraduate program’s standard operating procedures and is developed in consultation with undergraduate program leadership and faculty. An Academic Warning is sent out by the Registrar’s Office. The student is required to attend an Academic Progress Meeting during which a Learning Contract will be created with specific conditions tailored to the individual situation. The Registrar's Office will be informed as a matter of record and follow-up. ### Question 88: How can I get the information of campus usage for events so that I can have proper place to study without getting interrupted?  
### Answer: 

To get information about campus usage for events, you should contact the relevant administrative office or the student affairs department at your university. They typically manage schedules and can provide details on where events are being held and when, allowing you to find suitable places to study uninterrupted. Additionally, checking the university's official calendar or bulletin board can also be helpful. If specific areas like libraries or study rooms are reserved for events, these offices can guide you on alternative study locations. Always ensure to inquire well in advance to secure your preferred study spots.

### Question 89: I used to take an undergraduate program at another university and I want to transfer credit of studied courses at that university. What should I do?  
### Answer: 

To transfer credit of studied courses from another university to your Fulbright undergraduate degree, you should follow these steps:

1. Gather all the necessary information about the courses you wish to transfer, including the course curriculum, learning outcomes, course content, and assessments.

2. Submit an Application for Credit Transfer along with the required information on the course(s) to the Office of the Registrar.

3. The Registrar will coordinate with the Office of the Dean to determine whether credit or an exemption is justified based on the information provided.

4. Ensure that the courses you are transferring meet the requirements for your Fulbright undergraduate degree and are equivalent to courses offered at Fulbright.

5. Be aware that a maximum of 64 credit hours can be transferred and credited to a Fulbright undergraduate degree.

By following these steps, you can successfully apply for Credit Transfer and potentially earn credit towards your Fulbright undergraduate degree. If you have any questions or need further assistance, consult with your Academic/Major Advisor.

<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 10]

### Question 90: What are the policies of CWP?  
### Answer: 

The policies of CWP, as described in the given text, pertain to logistical support for capstone projects. Specifically, they state that if a capstone project requires logistical arrangements outside the university's typical academic scope, the student must notify the Psychology faculty and relevant Fulbright University functionaries well in advance. This applies to various scenarios such as events organized by the student in partnership with groups inside or outside Fulbright University Vietnam, applied projects taking place on the FUV campus (like organizing an exhibition or producing a documentary), and any project that might raise liability concerns for the student or the institution. These policies aim to ensure proper planning and management of such projects to avoid potential issues.

### Question 91: I'm a student athlete then how can I bypass all of physical education courses required to graduate?  
### Answer: 

As a student athlete, you can bypass the physical education courses required to graduate by taking Physical Education courses, which do not count toward the 128-credit requirement. Therefore, these courses will not impact your graduation requirements.

All students for whom English is not their first language must take an English Assessment Test required by NECHE Accreditation. 13.8  Double Counting In satisfying degree requirements, some courses can be double-counted. For example, an exploratory course can also be counted as a major course for the corresponding major. However, the number of double-counted credits is often limited (e.g., see subsections 13.2 and 13.3). Additionally, any particular course can only be used to satisfy at most two requirements. For instance, if course X is cross-listed between major A and major B and tagged by minor C, then X can be used to fulfill the requirements of major A and major B, or major A and minor C, or major B and minor C. Triple counting is not allowed. 13.9  Maximal Length of Study Fulbright follows MOET regulations, which state that the maximum time to complete the program cannot exceed double the standard

The second period starts after 4:00 PM Friday, Week 4 to 4:00 PM Friday, Week 8. Attempted credits and a “W” grade will be recorded on the transcript for the course(s) from which students withdraw in this period. This grade does not affect a student’s GPA. In order to withdraw from a course, students need to submit the Course Withdrawal form to the Registrar’s Office, following the above timeline. A student who withdraws from a course beyond the halfway point of that course (end of week 4 for an 8-week course or end of week 8 for a full-term course) automatically receives a grade of ‘F’, which will affect the student’s GPA. ### Question 92: I'm currently a third year student and moved out of university dormitory after first year but now I'm struggling to find a new accommodation so can I register again for dormitory and will I still have the financial support?  
### Answer: 

Based on the information provided, it seems that you are no longer a resident of the university dormitory since you moved out after your first year. Therefore, you would need to apply for housing through the university's housing office or waitlist if available. 

Regarding financial support, typically, financial aid is awarded based on the student's enrollment status and the number of credits they are registered for. Since you are a third-year student, you might already be eligible for financial aid. However, the availability of financial support for housing would depend on the specific policies of your university.

It is recommended that you contact the university's housing office and financial aid office directly to inquire about your options and eligibility for financial support. They will be able to provide you with more detailed and accurate information based on your individual situation. 

Please note that the information provided in the given text does not specifically address the issue of re-registering for dormitory accommodation or financial support for housing. Therefore, it is important to reach out to the relevant offices for personalized guidance.

### Question 94: How many ways are there provided by the university can I get the support in my academic path?  
### Answer: 

There are two ways provided by the university to get support in your academic path: mentorship and industry involvement, and allocation of advisor. 

Mentorship and Industry Involvement: Industry mentors may be available for project guidance, helping bridge academic learning and industry practice. They could be secondary advisors for Capstone projects, but not primary advisors or independent reviewers. They could also be invited to join the capstone panel. As either a secondary advisor or a member of the capstone panel, industry mentors could participate in grading.

Allocation of Advisor: Successful applicants will be matched to their first choice of primary and secondary advisor where possible. If the student’s first or second preference cannot be accommodated due to the necessity of maintaining a fair distribution of faculty workload, the major capstone coordinator will consult with the student to determine an appropriate solution.

### Question 97: I'm having some bad experience with a professor teaching a course. The problem was his way of delivering does not meet academic standard and I want to say something about this with people having higher authorities. What should I do?  
### Answer: 

Based on the provided context, you should follow these steps:

1. Discuss the issue directly with the course instructor(s) to address your concerns about the way the course is being delivered. This is the first step in resolving any issues related to a professor's teaching methods.

2. If the matter remains unresolved after discussing it with the instructor, and you believe there has been an error in grading, bias, or a failure to follow published grading policies, you can file an appeal.

3. To file an appeal, submit the Review of Final Grade Request form to the Registrar's Office within five business days from the date on which the final grade is posted.

4. The Registrar's Office will inform the Dean’s Office of the case. If the Deans can mediate, no further action is required. However, if mediation is not successful, the Registrar's Office will organize a panel review with the Dean’s Office for an independent evaluation of the grade.

5. The grade determined after this evaluation will be the final grade.

Remember, you need to provide appropriate documentation and contact your instructors to initiate arrangements to make up any missed work. Additionally, if you're seeking excused absences due to emergencies, you must obtain approval from the Office of the Dean and Deans of Students, ensuring you're in good academic standing and not on probation. 

By following these steps, you can escalate your concerns to the appropriate authorities while adhering to the institution's procedures.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 10]
• The Registrar's Office informs the Dean’s Office of the case. After investigation, if the Deans can mediate, no further action is required. Otherwise, the Registrar's Office organizes a panel review with the Dean’s Office for an independent evaluation of the grade. The grade determined after this evaluation shall be the final grade. In cases concerning the interpretation of a course policy, the Dean’s Office will defer to the course syllabus whenever possible and otherwise will make a final ruling on the matter.

### Question 98: I'm a third year student and don't know if I should do a capstone project then where should I go to get advice?  
### Answer: 

You should go to the major capstone coordinator to get advice on whether you should do a capstone project as a third-year student. They will help you consider your interests, post-graduation plans, and whether the capstone aligns with your goals. Additionally, they can provide guidance on finding an appropriate advisor and addressing any concerns about the feasibility of completing the capstone as a third-year student.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: History Capstone Handbook - 2025-26.pdf, Page: 9]
Your primary advisor may not be an expert on your chosen subject and almost certainly isn’t an expert on the narrow historical problem you will tackle in your Capstone project—and that is okay! The main role of your Capstone advisor is to guide you through the research process and to evaluate your mastery of that process, regardless of the topic. If you feel that you need expert guidance on a particular topic and that no one on our faculty has specialized knowledge on that topic, you may want to consider requesting an external secondary advisor who does. Another way to approach this is to propose a Capstone project based on a 300-level research seminar that you have taken at Fulbright, or to ask the faculty for topic suggestions—that way, you are more likely to end up with a primary advisor who is also a subject-matter expert! The History Capstone Handbook, AY2025-26 student wishing to pursue journalism may want to complete their project in the form of a film or podcast. In general, although there can be

[Source: SOCIAL STUDIES CAPSTONE HANDBOOK 2025-2026.pdf, Page: 13]
be accomodated when prudent. If the student’s first or second preference cannot be accommodated due to the necessity of maintaining a fair distribution of faculty workload, the major capstone coordinator will consult with the student to determine an appropriate solution. 1.3. Advising process The primary advisor is your first point of contact, and should hold expertise relevant to your project, for example, in terms of being a specialist in the project’s disciplinary field. The primary advisor will be the primary reviewer of your work in progress, and as such, will be the person with whom you meet most frequently.  Expertise does not need to be regional or topical – an advisor may have a strong grounding in the theory or methodological approaches of the capstone rather than a specific research background in that topic. The secondary advisor can offer you additional feedback where necessary and may represent a disciplinary field outside of Social Studies (if your project is interdisciplinary). In cases when

[Source: History Capstone Handbook - 2025-26.pdf, Page: 9]
The Capstone project is a year-long undertaking with less structure than a traditional course. It is certainly not the easiest way to complete your degree, and it may not be the most logical option for you, depending on your interests and your post-graduation plans. You should not consider it to be the default pathway to finishing your degree. One of the best reasons to undertake a Capstone project is if you enjoy doing historical research (which you will have sampled in Hands-On History and the research seminars you have completed) and want an opportunity to carry out a long-term research project. For such students, the Capstone year provides time and guidance that is unparalleled by any course or other opportunity at the undergraduate level. However, if you wish to graduate with distinction—an honorable goal— but you don’t particularly enjoy doing independent research, you may want to skip the Capstone and focus on GPA honors instead! Normally, the Capstone sequence begins in the Fall with Capstone I and

[Source: Integrated Sciences_Capstone Handbook_14Jan2025.pdf, Page: 12]
not to do the thinking and working in your place. Changes to the topic are possible but requires careful consideration and approval from the primary advisor. Note that: • You cannot change the research question / subjects/ key methodology (for example doing computation study vs wet lab) without consulting your advisors and getting their approval. • You should have clear understanding of what you are required to submit at certain stages of the project. If not, clarify with your advisor. 1.5. Capstone I In Capstone I you will commence the research and refine your project proposal and plan, secure necessary resources, and do preliminary training or work. Reseach in natural sciences requires significant preparation of samples, physical and/or computatational facilities, and other consumables such as chemicals. The sooner you get this done the better. Follow the instructions of your advisors for the detailed outputs required for capstone I. In general the process should be as follows. Refine your project proposal

be exceptions, both thesis and non-thesis Capstones should ‘work up’ sources that do not figure extensively in existing scholarship, rather than taking the form of a literature review or commentary on existing secondary sources. This is something to discuss with a potential advisor. Guidelines for the Capstone by Thesis are included in Section 3 of this handbook. If students propose a project in an alternative format, the History faculty will confer and establish guidelines for the new format. 1.7. There are other opportunities for group research. 1.8. Capstone I In Capstone I, you will actively conduct research and refine your project proposal and plan. ### Question 99: I'm a member of Fulbright Basketball Club and going to attend a tournament. I need the official transcript and asking for some absence in classes then where should I get help?  
### Answer: 

You should contact the faculty or supervising staff responsible for the basketball club to request a University Official Activity Excused Absence Request Form. They will submit this form to the Dean’s Office, keeping Academic Affairs and Registrar’s Office informed. Additionally, you should discuss any unplanned absence or any known conflict with your course instructors as soon as possible. Ensure you follow the instructions provided for making up any missed work. If you encounter any emergencies preventing you from following these steps, contact the Academic Affairs team or Registrar’s Office during business hours. Remember, you need to be in good academic standing and not on probation to be excused from the class. Fulbright is committed to supporting student learning when absences are unavoidable. For official transcript requests, you should contact the Registrar’s Office directly.

### Question 102: How to work with major report?  
### Answer: 

To work effectively on the major report for Capstone 2, follow these steps:

1. Define clear objectives for the project: Establish the goals and scope of your project. This will guide your work throughout the semester.

2. Conduct a thorough literature review: Research and summarize relevant studies and existing solutions related to your problem. This will help you understand the context and identify gaps in current knowledge.

3. Develop a detailed project plan and timeline: Outline the methods, approach, and activities you will undertake during Capstone 2. This will ensure you stay on track and meet deadlines.

4. Write the report: Include the following sections:
   - Introduction/Motivation for the problem: Introduce the problem and its significance.
   - Literature review: Summarize relevant research and existing solutions.
   - Problem statement/description: Clearly articulate the problem you are addressing.
   - Proposed methods, plan and timeline for Capstone 2: Propose the methods/approach and outline your activities for the next semester.

5. Submit the report: Ensure it meets the submission requirements, including the deadline and content guidelines.

6. Seek feedback: Share early drafts of your work with your advisors and peers to receive constructive feedback.

7. Prepare for the final defense: Arrange your final defense and obtain signatures on the necessary paperwork.

8. Address any issues: Discuss any problems you encounter with your advisors and seek solutions.

9. Follow up: Regularly communicate with your advisors and submit work-in-progress to them.

By following these steps, you will be able to produce a comprehensive and well-organized major report for Capstone 2. Remember to respect your advisor's working hours, correspond professionally, and manage your time effectively. Good luck!

### Question 103: How many way can I fill in the requirements of EL?  
### Answer: 

You can fulfill the Exploratory Learning (EL) requirements in multiple ways depending on your class year. For Class of 2024 students, you need to complete 16 credits (4 courses) with one course from each of the four categories: E1-Arts and Humanities, E2-Social Sciences, E3-Sciences and Engineering, and E4-Mathematics and Computing. At most, 4 out of these 16 credits can be counted as Pass/No Pass. For students from Classes of 2025, 2026, and 2027, you need to complete 32 credits (8 courses), with eight credits from each category, and again, at most 4 out of these 32 credits can be counted as Pass/No Pass. 

Remember, you should aim to complete these requirements by the end of your second year. Also, note that if you have more than one major, the 8-credit limit is independently applied to each major. This means you would need to meet the EL requirements separately for each major you pursue. The information provided does not specify how many ways there are to fill in the requirements, but it does outline the structure and constraints of the Exploratory Learning requirements. Therefore, the number of ways to fulfill these requirements depends on your personal choice of courses within the specified categories and credit limits.
